<p><b>Cape Verde</b> <span class="nowrap"><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/</a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="/Àå/ secondary stress follows" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">Àå</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="'k' in 'kind'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">k</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="/e…™/ long 'a' in 'base'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">e…™</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="'p' in 'pie'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">p</span></a></span> <span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="/Àà/ primary stress follows" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">Àà</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="'v' in 'vie'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">v</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="/…úr/ 'ir' in 'bird'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">…úr</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="'d' in 'dye'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">d</span></a></span><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/</a></span></span> or <b>Cabo Verde</b> <span class="nowrap"><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/</a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="'k' in 'kind'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">k</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="/aÀê/ variable 'a' in 'bath'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">aÀê</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="'b' in 'buy'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">b</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="/o ä/ long 'o' in 'bode'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">o ä</span></a></span> <span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="/Àà/ primary stress follows" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">Àà</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="'v' in 'vie'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">v</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="/…úr/ 'ir' in 'bird'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">…úr</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="'d' in 'dye'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">d</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="/e…™/ long 'a' in 'base'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">e…™</span></a></span><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/</a></span></span> (<a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>: <span lang="pt"><i>Cabo Verde</i></span>, <small>pronounced:&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Portuguese_and_Galician" title="Help:IPA for Portuguese and Galician">[Ààkabu Ààve…æd…®]</a></span>), officially the <b>Republic of Cabo Verde</b>,<sup id="cite_ref-NameNatGeo_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NameNatGeo-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> is an <a href="/wiki/Island_country" title="Island country">island country</a> spanning an <a href="/wiki/Archipelago" title="Archipelago">archipelago</a> of 10 volcanic islands in the central <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a>. Located 570 kilometres (350&#160;mi) off the coast of Western Africa, the islands cover a combined area of slightly over 4,000 square kilometres (1,500&#160;sq&#160;mi).</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portuguese</a> explorers discovered and <a href="/wiki/Colony" title="Colony">colonized</a> the uninhabited islands in the 15th century, the first European settlement in the tropics. Ideally located for the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_slave_trade" title="Atlantic slave trade">Atlantic slave trade</a>, the islands grew prosperous and often attracted <a href="/wiki/Privateer" title="Privateer">privateers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Piracy" title="Piracy">pirates</a>, among them Sir <a href="/wiki/Francis_Drake" title="Francis Drake">Francis Drake</a> in the 1580s. The islands were also visited by <a href="/wiki/Charles_Darwin" title="Charles Darwin">Charles Darwin</a> during <a href="/wiki/Robert_FitzRoy" title="Robert FitzRoy">FitzRoy's</a> <a href="/wiki/HMS_Beagle" title="HMS Beagle"><i>Beagle</i></a> voyage in 1832. The islands were settled as the colony grew in importance on the main shipping lanes from Europe to India and Australia, and population increased steadily.</p>
<p>At the time of independence from Portugal in 1975, Cape Verdeans emigrated across the world, such that the population in the 21st century of over half a million people on the islands is equaled by the diaspora in Europe, the Americas, and on the African continent. The Cape Verdean economy is mostly service-oriented with a growing focus on tourism and foreign investment.</p>
<p>The country is known for the <a href="/wiki/Cape_Verde-type_hurricane" title="Cape Verde-type hurricane">Cape Verdean type hurricanes</a> that form off the coast of the archipelago islands. While many move harmlessly out to sea, some move across the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">Caribbean Sea</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico" title="Gulf of Mexico">Gulf of Mexico</a>, becoming damaging storms for Caribbean nations, Central America, Mexico, <a href="/wiki/Bermuda" title="Bermuda">Bermuda</a>, the United States, and occasionally even Canada.</p>
<p>Historically, the name "Cape Verde" has been used in English for the archipelago and, since independence in 1975, for the country. In 2013, the Cape Verdean government determined that the Portuguese designation "Cabo Verde" would henceforth be used for official purposes, such as at the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, even in English contexts.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Verde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The name of the country stems from the nearby <a href="/wiki/Cap-Vert" title="Cap-Vert">Cap-Vert</a>, on the <a href="/wiki/Senegal" title="Senegal">Senegalese</a> coast,<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> which in its turn was originally named "Cabo Verde" when it was sighted by Portuguese explorers in 1444, a few years before the islands were discovered (<i>verde</i> is <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a> for "green").</p>
<p>On 24 October 2013 it was announced at the United Nations that the official name should no longer be translated into other languages. Instead of "Cape Verde", the designation "Republic of Cabo Verde" is to be used.<sup id="cite_ref-NameNatGeo_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NameNatGeo-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Verde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Cape_Verde" title="History of Cape Verde">History of Cape Verde</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Insulae_Capitis_viridis-1598.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Insulae_Capitis_viridis-1598.jpg/300px-Insulae_Capitis_viridis-1598.jpg" width="300" height="214" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Insulae_Capitis_viridis-1598.jpg/450px-Insulae_Capitis_viridis-1598.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Insulae_Capitis_viridis-1598.jpg/600px-Insulae_Capitis_viridis-1598.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1438" data-file-height="1024" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Insulae_Capitis_viridis-1598.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i>Insulae Capitis Viridis</i> (1598), showing Cape Verde.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mindelo-MontCara2000.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Mindelo-MontCara2000.jpg/250px-Mindelo-MontCara2000.jpg" width="250" height="111" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Mindelo-MontCara2000.jpg/375px-Mindelo-MontCara2000.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Mindelo-MontCara2000.jpg/500px-Mindelo-MontCara2000.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3112" data-file-height="1378" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mindelo-MontCara2000.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A view of <a href="/wiki/Monte_Cara" title="Monte Cara">Monte Cara</a> from <a href="/wiki/Mindelo" title="Mindelo">Mindelo</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Before the arrival of Europeans, the Cape Verde Islands were uninhabited. The islands of the Cape Verde archipelago were discovered by <a href="/wiki/Genoa" title="Genoa">Genoese</a> and Portuguese <a href="/wiki/Navigator" title="Navigator">navigators</a> around 1456. According to Portuguese official records,<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> the first discoveries were made by <a href="/wiki/Genoa" title="Genoa">Genoa</a>-born <a href="/wiki/Ant%C3%B3nio_de_Noli" title="Ant√≥nio de Noli">Ant√≥nio de Noli</a>, who was afterwards appointed governor of Cape Verde by Portuguese <a href="/wiki/Afonso_V_of_Portugal" title="Afonso V of Portugal">King Afonso V</a>. Other navigators mentioned as contributing to discoveries in the Cape Verde archipelago are <a href="/wiki/Diogo_Gomes" title="Diogo Gomes">Diogo Gomes</a> (who was with Ant√≥nio de Noli and claimed to have been the first to land on and name Santiago island), <a href="/wiki/Diogo_Dias" title="Diogo Dias">Diogo Dias</a>, Diogo Afonso and the Italian (Venice-born) <a href="/wiki/Alvise_Cadamosto" title="Alvise Cadamosto">Alvise Cadamosto</a>.</p>
<p>In 1462, Portuguese settlers arrived at <a href="/wiki/Santiago,_Cape_Verde" title="Santiago, Cape Verde">Santiago</a> and founded a settlement they called Ribeira Grande (now called <a href="/wiki/Cidade_Velha" title="Cidade Velha">Cidade Velha</a>, to avoid being confused with the town of <a href="/wiki/Ribeira_Grande,_Cape_Verde" title="Ribeira Grande, Cape Verde">Ribeira Grande</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Santo_Ant%C3%A3o,_Cape_Verde" title="Santo Ant√£o, Cape Verde">Santo Ant√£o</a> island). Ribeira Grande was the first permanent European settlement in the <a href="/wiki/Tropics" title="Tropics">tropics</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bn_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bn-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In the 16th century, the archipelago prospered from the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_slave_trade" title="Atlantic slave trade">Atlantic slave trade</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bn_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bn-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> Pirates occasionally attacked the Portuguese settlements. Sir <a href="/wiki/Francis_Drake" title="Francis Drake">Francis Drake</a>, an English corsair <a href="/wiki/Privateer" title="Privateer">privateering</a> under a <a href="/wiki/Letter_of_marque" title="Letter of marque">letter of marque</a> granted by the English crown, twice sacked the (then) capital <a href="/wiki/Cidade_Velha" title="Cidade Velha">Ribeira Grande</a> in 1585.<sup id="cite_ref-bn_9-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bn-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> After a French attack in 1712, the town declined in importance relative to nearby <a href="/wiki/Praia" title="Praia">Praia</a>, which became the capital in 1770.<sup id="cite_ref-bn_9-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bn-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Decline in the slave trade in the 19th century resulted in an economic crisis. Cape Verde's early prosperity slowly vanished. However, the islands' position astride mid-Atlantic shipping lanes made Cape Verde an ideal location for re-supplying ships. Because of its excellent harbour, <a href="/wiki/Mindelo" title="Mindelo">Mindelo</a> (on the island of <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Vicente,_Cape_Verde" title="S√£o Vicente, Cape Verde">S√£o Vicente</a>) became an important commercial centre during the 19th century.<sup id="cite_ref-bn_9-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bn-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> Diplomat <a href="/wiki/Edmund_Roberts_(diplomat)" title="Edmund Roberts (diplomat)">Edmund Roberts</a> visited Cape Verde in 1832.<sup id="cite_ref-Roberts_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Roberts-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>With few natural resources and inadequate sustainable investment from the Portuguese, the citizens grew increasingly discontented with the colonial masters, who nevertheless refused to provide the local authorities with more autonomy. In 1951, Portugal changed Cape Verde's status from a colony to an overseas province in an attempt to blunt growing <a href="/wiki/Nationalism" title="Nationalism">nationalism</a>. In 1956, <a href="/wiki/Am%C3%ADlcar_Cabral" title="Am√≠lcar Cabral">Am√≠lcar Cabral</a> and a group of fellow Cape Verdeans and Guineans organised (in <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Guinea" title="Portuguese Guinea">Portuguese Guinea</a>) the clandestine <a href="/wiki/African_Party_for_the_Independence_of_Guinea_and_Cape_Verde" title="African Party for the Independence of Guinea and Cape Verde">African Party for the Independence of Guinea and Cape Verde</a> (PAIGC).<sup id="cite_ref-bn_9-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bn-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>It demanded improvement in economic, social and political conditions in Cape Verde and Portuguese Guinea and formed the basis of the two nations' independence movement. Moving its headquarters to <a href="/wiki/Conakry" title="Conakry">Conakry</a>, Guinea in 1960, the PAIGC began an armed rebellion against Portugal in 1961. Acts of sabotage eventually grew into a <a href="/wiki/Guinea-Bissau_War_of_Independence" title="Guinea-Bissau War of Independence">war in Portuguese Guinea</a> that pitted 10,000 <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Bloc" title="Eastern Bloc">Soviet Bloc</a>-supported PAIGC soldiers against 35,000 Portuguese and African troops.<sup id="cite_ref-bn_9-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bn-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Cape_Verde_(1975-1992).svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Flag_of_Cape_Verde_%281975-1992%29.svg/250px-Flag_of_Cape_Verde_%281975-1992%29.svg.png" width="250" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Flag_of_Cape_Verde_%281975-1992%29.svg/375px-Flag_of_Cape_Verde_%281975-1992%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Flag_of_Cape_Verde_%281975-1992%29.svg/500px-Flag_of_Cape_Verde_%281975-1992%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="400" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Cape_Verde_(1975-1992).svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The first national flag of Cape Verde.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>By 1972, the PAIGC controlled much of Portuguese Guinea despite the presence of the Portuguese troops, but the organization did not attempt to disrupt Portuguese control in Cape Verde. Portuguese Guinea declared independence in 1973 and was granted <a href="/wiki/De_jure" title="De jure">de jure</a> independence in 1974. A budding independence movement&#160;‚Äî originally led by <a href="/wiki/Am%C3%ADlcar_Cabral" title="Am√≠lcar Cabral">Am√≠lcar Cabral</a>, assassinated in 1973&#160;‚Äî passed on to his half-brother <a href="/wiki/Lu%C3%ADs_Cabral" title="Lu√≠s Cabral">Lu√≠s Cabral</a> and culminated in independence for the archipelago in 1975.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Independence_.281975.29">Independence (1975)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Verde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Independence (1975)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Following the <a href="/wiki/Carnation_Revolution" title="Carnation Revolution">April 1974 revolution in Portugal</a>, the PAIGC became an active political movement in Cape Verde. In December 1974, the PAIGC and Portugal signed an agreement providing for a transitional government composed of Portuguese and Cape Verdeans. On 30 June 1975, Cape Verdeans elected a National Assembly which received the instruments of independence from Portugal on July 5, 1975.<sup id="cite_ref-bn_9-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bn-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> In the late 1970s and 1980s, most African countries prohibited <a href="/wiki/South_African_Airways" title="South African Airways">South African Airways</a> from overflights but Cape Verde allowed them and became a centre of activity for the airline's flights to Europe and the United States.</p>
<p>Immediately following the <a href="/wiki/History_of_Guinea-Bissau#Independence_from_Portugal" title="History of Guinea-Bissau">November 1980 coup in Guinea-Bissau</a>, relations between Cape Verde and Guinea-Bissau became strained. Cape Verde abandoned its hope for unity with Guinea-Bissau and formed the <a href="/wiki/African_Party_for_the_Independence_of_Cape_Verde" title="African Party for the Independence of Cape Verde">African Party for the Independence of Cape Verde</a> (PAICV). Problems have since been resolved and relations between the countries are good. The PAICV and its predecessor established a one-party system and ruled Cape Verde from independence until 1990.<sup id="cite_ref-bn_9-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bn-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Responding to growing pressure for pluralistic democracy, the PAICV called an emergency congress in February 1990 to discuss proposed constitutional changes to end one-party rule. Opposition groups came together to form the <a href="/wiki/Movement_for_Democracy_(Cape_Verde)" title="Movement for Democracy (Cape Verde)">Movement for Democracy</a> (MPD) in Praia in April 1990. Together, they campaigned for the right to contest the presidential election scheduled for December 1990.</p>
<p>The one-party state was abolished 28 September 1990, and the first multi-party elections were held in January 1991. The MPD won a majority of the seats in the National Assembly, and MPD presidential candidate <a href="/wiki/Ant%C3%B3nio_Mascarenhas_Monteiro" title="Ant√≥nio Mascarenhas Monteiro">Ant√≥nio Mascarenhas Monteiro</a> defeated the PAICV's candidate with 73.5% of the votes. Legislative elections in December 1995 increased the MPD majority in the National Assembly. The party won 50 of the National Assembly's 72 seats.</p>
<p>A February 1996 presidential election returned President Monteiro to office. Legislative elections in January 2001 returned power to the PAICV, with the PAICV holding 40 of the National Assembly seats, MPD 30, and <a href="/wiki/Party_for_Democratic_Convergence" title="Party for Democratic Convergence" class="mw-redirect">Party for Democratic Convergence</a> (PCD) and <a href="/wiki/Labour_and_Solidarity_Party" title="Labour and Solidarity Party">Labour and Solidarity Party</a> (PTS) 1 each. In February 2001, the PAICV-supported presidential candidate <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Pires" title="Pedro Pires">Pedro Pires</a> defeated former MPD leader <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Veiga" title="Carlos Veiga">Carlos Veiga</a> by only 13 votes.<sup id="cite_ref-bn_9-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bn-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Verde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Cape_Verde" title="Politics of Cape Verde">Politics of Cape Verde</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Secretary_of_Defense_Chuck_Hagel,_right,_escorts_Cape_Verde_Prime_Minister_Jose_Maria_Neves_through_an_honor_cordon_and_into_the_Pentagon_on_March_28,_2013_130328-D-TT977-063.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Secretary_of_Defense_Chuck_Hagel%2C_right%2C_escorts_Cape_Verde_Prime_Minister_Jose_Maria_Neves_through_an_honor_cordon_and_into_the_Pentagon_on_March_28%2C_2013_130328-D-TT977-063.jpg/250px-thumbnail.jpg" width="250" height="166" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Secretary_of_Defense_Chuck_Hagel%2C_right%2C_escorts_Cape_Verde_Prime_Minister_Jose_Maria_Neves_through_an_honor_cordon_and_into_the_Pentagon_on_March_28%2C_2013_130328-D-TT977-063.jpg/375px-thumbnail.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Secretary_of_Defense_Chuck_Hagel%2C_right%2C_escorts_Cape_Verde_Prime_Minister_Jose_Maria_Neves_through_an_honor_cordon_and_into_the_Pentagon_on_March_28%2C_2013_130328-D-TT977-063.jpg/500px-thumbnail.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3145" data-file-height="2093" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Secretary_of_Defense_Chuck_Hagel,_right,_escorts_Cape_Verde_Prime_Minister_Jose_Maria_Neves_through_an_honor_cordon_and_into_the_Pentagon_on_March_28,_2013_130328-D-TT977-063.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Cape Verdean Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Maria_Neves" title="Jos√© Maria Neves">Jos√© Maria Neves</a> meets with the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">U.S.</a> Secretary of Defense <a href="/wiki/Chuck_Hagel" title="Chuck Hagel">Chuck Hagel</a>, in 2013.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Cape Verde is a stable <a href="/wiki/Semi-presidential_system" title="Semi-presidential system">semi-presidential</a> <a href="/wiki/Representative_democracy" title="Representative democracy">representative democratic</a> <a href="/wiki/Republic" title="Republic">republic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-SP-L_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SP-L-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-constitution_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-constitution-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> It is among the most democratic nations in the world, ranking 31st position in the world, according to the <i>2014 Democracy Index</i> .<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> The constitution&#160;‚Äî adopted in 1980 and revised in 1992, 1995 and 1999&#160;‚Äî defines the basic principles of its government. The <a href="/wiki/President_of_Cape_Verde" title="President of Cape Verde" class="mw-redirect">president</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a> and is elected by <a href="/wiki/Popular_vote" title="Popular vote" class="mw-redirect">popular vote</a> for a 5-year term.<sup id="cite_ref-bn_9-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bn-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Cape_Verde" title="Prime Minister of Cape Verde" class="mw-redirect">prime minister</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a> and proposes other ministers and secretaries of state. The prime minister is nominated by the <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_(Cape_Verde)" title="National Assembly (Cape Verde)">National Assembly</a> and appointed by the president. Members of the National Assembly are elected by popular vote for 5-year terms. Three parties now hold seats in the National Assembly&#160;‚Äî PAICV (40), MPD (30), and Cape Verdean Independent Democratic Union (UCID) (2).<sup id="cite_ref-bn_9-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bn-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The judicial system consists of a Supreme Court of Justice&#160;‚Äî whose members are appointed by the president, the National Assembly, and the Board of the Judiciary&#160;‚Äî and regional courts. Separate courts hear civil, constitutional, and criminal cases. Appeal is to the Supreme Court.<sup id="cite_ref-bn_9-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bn-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Verde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Cape_Verde" title="Foreign relations of Cape Verde">Foreign relations of Cape Verde</a></div>
<p>Cape Verde follows a policy of <a href="/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement" title="Non-Aligned Movement">nonalignment</a> and seeks cooperative relations with all friendly states.<sup id="cite_ref-bn_9-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bn-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Angola" title="Angola">Angola</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>, the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="People's Republic of China" class="mw-redirect">People's Republic of China</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a>, <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Senegal" title="Senegal">Senegal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg" title="Luxembourg">Luxembourg</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> maintain embassies in <a href="/wiki/Praia" title="Praia">Praia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bn_9-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bn-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> Cape Verde is actively interested in foreign affairs, especially in Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-bn_9-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bn-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Cape Verde has <a href="/wiki/Bilateralism" title="Bilateralism">bilateral relations</a> with some <a href="/wiki/Lusophone" title="Lusophone">Lusophone</a> nations and holds membership in a number of international organisations.<sup id="cite_ref-bn_9-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bn-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> It also participates in most international conferences on economic and political issues.<sup id="cite_ref-bn_9-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bn-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> Since 2007, Cape Verde has a <i>special partnership</i> status<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> with the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">EU</a>, under the <a href="/wiki/Cotonou_Agreement" title="Cotonou Agreement">Cotonou Agreement</a>, and might apply for <a href="/wiki/Future_enlargement_of_the_European_Union#Cape_Verde" title="Future enlargement of the European Union">special membership</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2011 Cape Verde ratified the <a href="/wiki/Rome_Statute_of_the_International_Criminal_Court" title="Rome Statute of the International Criminal Court">Rome Statute of the International Criminal Court</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Verde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Cabo_Verdean_Armed_Forces" title="Cabo Verdean Armed Forces">Cabo Verdean Armed Forces</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Cabo_Verdean_Armed_Forces" title="Cabo Verdean Armed Forces">military of Cape Verde</a> consists of a coast guard and an army; 0.7% of the country's GDP was spent on the military in 2005.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="International_recognition">International recognition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Verde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: International recognition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Cape Verde is often praised as an example among African nations, for its stability and developmental growth despite its lack of natural resources. Among others, it has been recognized with the following assessments:</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Verde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Cape_Verde" title="Geography of Cape Verde">Geography of Cape Verde</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Topographic_map_of_Cape_Verde-en.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Topographic_map_of_Cape_Verde-en.svg/350px-Topographic_map_of_Cape_Verde-en.svg.png" width="350" height="260" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Topographic_map_of_Cape_Verde-en.svg/525px-Topographic_map_of_Cape_Verde-en.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Topographic_map_of_Cape_Verde-en.svg/700px-Topographic_map_of_Cape_Verde-en.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1464" data-file-height="1087" /></a>

</div>
</div>
<p>The Cape Verde archipelago is located in the Atlantic Ocean, approximately 570 kilometres (350&#160;mi) off the coast of West Africa, near <a href="/wiki/Senegal" title="Senegal">Senegal</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Gambia" title="The Gambia">The Gambia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mauritania" title="Mauritania">Mauritania</a>, and is part of the <a href="/wiki/Macaronesia" title="Macaronesia">Macaronesia</a> <a href="/wiki/Ecoregion" title="Ecoregion">ecoregion</a>. It lies between latitudes <a href="/wiki/14th_parallel_north" title="14th parallel north">14¬∞</a> and <a href="/wiki/18th_parallel_north" title="18th parallel north">18¬∞N</a>, and longitudes <a href="/wiki/22nd_meridian_west" title="22nd meridian west">22¬∞</a> and <a href="/wiki/26th_meridian_west" title="26th meridian west">26¬∞W</a>.</p>
<p>The country is a horseshoe-shaped cluster of ten islands (nine inhabited) and eight islets,<sup id="cite_ref-pc_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pc-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup> that constitute an area of 4033&#160;km<sup>2</sup>.<sup id="cite_ref-pc_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pc-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The islands are spatially divided into two groups:</p>
<ul>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Barlavento_Islands" title="Barlavento Islands">Barlavento Islands</a> (<a href="/wiki/Windward_and_leeward" title="Windward and leeward">windward</a> islands): <a href="/wiki/Santo_Ant%C3%A3o,_Cape_Verde" title="Santo Ant√£o, Cape Verde">Santo Ant√£o</a>, <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Vicente,_Cape_Verde" title="S√£o Vicente, Cape Verde">S√£o Vicente</a>, <a href="/wiki/Santa_Luzia,_Cape_Verde" title="Santa Luzia, Cape Verde">Santa Luzia</a>, <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Nicolau,_Cape_Verde" title="S√£o Nicolau, Cape Verde">S√£o Nicolau</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sal,_Cape_Verde" title="Sal, Cape Verde">Sal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boa_Vista,_Cape_Verde" title="Boa Vista, Cape Verde">Boa Vista</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-pc_19-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pc-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup> and</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Sotavento_Islands" title="Sotavento Islands">Sotavento Islands</a> (<a href="/wiki/Windward_and_leeward" title="Windward and leeward">leeward</a>): <a href="/wiki/Maio,_Cape_Verde" title="Maio, Cape Verde">Maio</a>, <a href="/wiki/Santiago,_Cape_Verde" title="Santiago, Cape Verde">Santiago</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fogo,_Cape_Verde" title="Fogo, Cape Verde">Fogo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brava,_Cape_Verde" title="Brava, Cape Verde">Brava</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-pc_19-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pc-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
<p>The largest island, both in size and population, is <a href="/wiki/Santiago,_Cape_Verde" title="Santiago, Cape Verde">Santiago</a>, which hosts the nation's capital, <a href="/wiki/Praia" title="Praia">Praia</a>, the principal agglomeration in the archipelago.<sup id="cite_ref-pc_19-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pc-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Three (<a href="/wiki/Sal,_Cape_Verde" title="Sal, Cape Verde">Sal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boa_Vista,_Cape_Verde" title="Boa Vista, Cape Verde">Boa Vista</a> and <a href="/wiki/Maio,_Cape_Verde" title="Maio, Cape Verde">Maio</a>) are fairly flat, sandy and dry; the others are generally rockier with more vegetation.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Physical_geography_and_geology">Physical geography and geology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Verde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Physical geography and geology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Geologically, the islands, covering a combined area of slightly over 4,033 square kilometres (1,557&#160;sq&#160;mi), are principally composed of <a href="/wiki/Igneous_rock" title="Igneous rock">igneous rocks</a>, with volcanic structures and <a href="/wiki/Pyroclastic_rock" title="Pyroclastic rock">pyroclastic</a> debris comprising the majority of the archipelago's total volume. The <a href="/wiki/Volcano" title="Volcano">volcanic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pluton" title="Pluton">plutonic rocks</a> are distinctly basic; the archipelago is a soda-alkaline <a href="/wiki/Petrography" title="Petrography">petrographic</a> province, with a <a href="/wiki/Petrology" title="Petrology">petrologic</a> succession similar to that found in other <a href="/wiki/Macaronesia" title="Macaronesia">Macaronesian</a> islands.</p>
<p>Magnetic anomalies identified in the vicinity of the archipelago indicate that the structures forming the islands date back 125-150 million years: the islands themselves date from 8 million (in the west) to 20 million years (in the east).<sup id="cite_ref-Pim_et_al..2C_2008.2C_p.422_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pim_et_al..2C_2008.2C_p.422-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> The oldest exposed rocks occurred on Maio and northern peninsula of Santiago and are 128-131 million year old pillow lavas. The first stage of volcanism in the islands began in the early <a href="/wiki/Miocene" title="Miocene">Miocene</a>, and reached its peak at the end of this period, when the islands reached their maximum sizes. Historical volcanism (within human settlement) has been restricted to the island of Fogo.</p>
<p>The origin of the islands' volcanism has been attributed to a <a href="/wiki/Hotspot_(geology)" title="Hotspot (geology)">hotspot</a>, associated with bathymetric swell that formed the Cape Verde Rise.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> The Rise is one of the largest protuberances in the world's oceans, rising 2.2 kilometers in a semi-circular region of 1200&#160;km<sup>2</sup>, associated with a rise of the <a href="/wiki/Geoid" title="Geoid">geoid</a> and elevated surface heat flow.<sup id="cite_ref-Pim_et_al..2C_2008.2C_p.422_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pim_et_al..2C_2008.2C_p.422-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Most recently erupting in 2014, <a href="/wiki/Pico_do_Fogo" title="Pico do Fogo">Pico do Fogo</a> is the largest active <a href="/wiki/Volcano" title="Volcano">volcano</a> in the region. It has a 8&#160;km (5&#160;mi) diameter <a href="/wiki/Caldera" title="Caldera">caldera</a>, whose rim is 1,600&#160;m (5,249&#160;ft) altitude and an interior cone that rises to 2,829&#160;m (9,281&#160;ft) above sea level. The caldera resulted from subsidence, following the partial evacuation (eruption) of the <a href="/wiki/Magma" title="Magma">magma</a> chamber, along a cylindrical column from within magma chamber (at a depth of 8&#160;km (5&#160;mi)).</p>
<p>Extensive <a href="/wiki/Salt_pan_(geology)" title="Salt pan (geology)">salt flats</a> are found on Sal and Maio.<sup id="cite_ref-pc_19-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pc-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup> On Santiago, Santo Ant√£o, and S√£o Nicolau, arid slopes give way in places to sugarcane fields or banana plantations spread along the base of towering mountains.<sup id="cite_ref-pc_19-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pc-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup> Ocean cliffs have been formed by catastrophic <a href="/wiki/Landslide#Debris_landslide" title="Landslide">debris landslides</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>According to the president of <a href="/wiki/Nauru" title="Nauru">Nauru</a>, Cape Verde has been ranked the eighth most endangered nation due to flooding from <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">climate change</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Verde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Cape_Verde#Climate" title="Geography of Cape Verde">Geography of Cape Verde ¬ß Climate</a></div>
<p>Cape Verde's climate is milder than that of the African mainland, because the surrounding sea moderates temperatures on the islands and cold Atlantic currents produces an arid atmosphere around the archipelago. Conversely, the islands do not receive the upwellings (cold streams) that affect the West African coast, so the air temperature is cooler than in Senegal, but the sea is actually warmer, because the orographic relief of some islands, such as Santiago with steep mountains, cover it with rich woods and luxuriant vegetation where the humid air condenses and soak the plants, rocks, soil, logs, moss, etc. On the higher islands and somewhat wetter islands, exclusively in mountainous areas, like Santo Ant√£o island, the climate is suitable for the development of dry monsoon forest, and laurel forest as this vegetation<sup id="cite_ref-pc_19-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pc-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup> Average daily high temperatures range from 23&#160;¬∞C (73&#160;¬∞F) in February to 29&#160;¬∞C (84.2&#160;¬∞F) in September.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Cape Verde is part of the <a href="/wiki/Sahel" title="Sahel">Sahelian arid belt</a>, with nothing like the rainfall levels of nearby West Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-pc_19-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pc-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup> It does rain irregularly between August and October, with frequent brief-but-heavy downpours.<sup id="cite_ref-pc_19-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pc-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup> A <i>desert</i> is usually defined as terrain that receives less than 250&#160;mm (9.8&#160;in) of annual rainfall. Cape Verde's total (265&#160;mm (10.4&#160;in)) is slightly above this criterion, which makes the area climate <i><a href="/wiki/Semi-desert" title="Semi-desert" class="mw-redirect">semi-desert</a></i>.</p>

<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:237px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cape_Verde.2010-11-23.250m-per-px.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Cape_Verde.2010-11-23.250m-per-px.jpg/235px-Cape_Verde.2010-11-23.250m-per-px.jpg" width="235" height="185" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Cape_Verde.2010-11-23.250m-per-px.jpg/353px-Cape_Verde.2010-11-23.250m-per-px.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Cape_Verde.2010-11-23.250m-per-px.jpg/470px-Cape_Verde.2010-11-23.250m-per-px.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2800" data-file-height="2200" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cape_Verde.2010-11-23.250m-per-px.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A satellite photo of the Cape Verde islands, 2010.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Sal,_Cape_Verde" title="Sal, Cape Verde">Sal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boa_Vista,_Cape_Verde" title="Boa Vista, Cape Verde">Boa Vista</a> and <a href="/wiki/Maio,_Cape_Verde" title="Maio, Cape Verde">Maio</a> have a flat landscape and arid climate, the remaining ones are generally rockier and have more vegetation. Because of the infrequent occurrence of rainfall the overall landscape is not particularly green. The archipelago can be divided into four broad ecological zones&#160;‚Äî arid, semiarid, subhumid and humid, according to altitude and average annual rainfall ranging from 200&#160;mm in the arid areas of the coast to more than 1000&#160;mm in the humid mountain. Most rainfall precipitation is due to condensation of the ocean mist.</p>
<p>In some islands, as <a href="/wiki/Santiago,_Cape_Verde" title="Santiago, Cape Verde">Santiago</a>, the wetter climate of the interior and the eastern coast contrasts with the dryer one in the south/southwest coast. <a href="/wiki/Praia" title="Praia">Praia</a>, on the southeast coast, is the largest city of the island and the largest city and capital of the country.</p>
<p>Because of their proximity to the Sahara, most of the Cape Verde islands are dry, but on islands with high mountains and farther away from the coast, by orography, the humidity is much higher, providing a rainforest habitat, although much affected by the human presence. Northeastern slopes of high mountains often receive a lot of rain while southwest slopes do not. These umbria areas are identified with cool and moisture.</p>
<p>Hurricanes that form near the Cape Verde Islands are sometimes referred to as <a href="/wiki/Cape_Verde-type_hurricane" title="Cape Verde-type hurricane">Cape Verde-type hurricanes</a>. These hurricanes can become very intense as they cross warm Atlantic waters. The average hurricane season has about two Cape Verde-type hurricanes, which are usually the largest and most intense storms of the season because they often have plenty of warm open ocean over which to develop before encountering land. The five largest Atlantic tropical cyclones on record have been Cape Verde-type hurricanes. Most of the longest-lived tropical cyclones in the Atlantic basin are Cape Verde hurricanes.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Biome">Biome</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Verde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Biome">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_Cape_Verde" title="Wildlife of Cape Verde">Wildlife of Cape Verde</a></div>
<p>Cape Verde's isolation has resulted in the islands having a number of <a href="/wiki/Endemic_(ecology)" title="Endemic (ecology)" class="mw-redirect">endemic</a> <a href="/wiki/Species" title="Species">species</a>, particularly bird and reptiles, many of which are <a href="/wiki/Endangered_species" title="Endangered species">endangered</a> by human development. Endemic birds include <a href="/wiki/Alexander%27s_swift" title="Alexander's swift" class="mw-redirect">Alexander's swift</a> (<i>Apus alexandri</i>), <a href="/wiki/Bourne%27s_heron" title="Bourne's heron">Bourne's heron</a> (<i>Ardea purpurea bournei</i>), the <a href="/wiki/Raso_lark" title="Raso lark">Raso lark</a> (<i>Alauda razae</i>), the <a href="/wiki/Cape_Verde_warbler" title="Cape Verde warbler">Cape Verde warbler</a> (<i>Acrocephalus brevipennis</i>), and the <a href="/wiki/Iago_sparrow" title="Iago sparrow">Iago sparrow</a> (<i>Passer iagoensis</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> The islands are also an important breeding area for seabirds including the <a href="/wiki/Cape_Verde_shearwater" title="Cape Verde shearwater">Cape Verde shearwater</a>. Reptiles include the Cape Verde giant gecko (<i><a href="/wiki/Tarentola" title="Tarentola">Tarentola</a> gigas</i>).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Verde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<p><br style="clear:both;" /></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Verde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Cape_Verde" title="Economy of Cape Verde">Economy of Cape Verde</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tree_map_export_2009_Cape_Verde.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Tree_map_export_2009_Cape_Verde.jpeg/350px-Tree_map_export_2009_Cape_Verde.jpeg" width="350" height="273" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Tree_map_export_2009_Cape_Verde.jpeg/525px-Tree_map_export_2009_Cape_Verde.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Tree_map_export_2009_Cape_Verde.jpeg/700px-Tree_map_export_2009_Cape_Verde.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="1106" data-file-height="863" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tree_map_export_2009_Cape_Verde.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A proportional representation of Cape Verde's export products.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Praia-March%C3%A9.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Praia-March%C3%A9.jpg/300px-Praia-March%C3%A9.jpg" width="300" height="225" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Praia-March%C3%A9.jpg/450px-Praia-March%C3%A9.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Praia-March%C3%A9.jpg/600px-Praia-March%C3%A9.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2736" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Praia-March%C3%A9.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A market in the capital Praia.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cape_Verde_Sal_pool.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Cape_Verde_Sal_pool.jpg/300px-Cape_Verde_Sal_pool.jpg" width="300" height="202" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Cape_Verde_Sal_pool.jpg/450px-Cape_Verde_Sal_pool.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Cape_Verde_Sal_pool.jpg/600px-Cape_Verde_Sal_pool.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4212" data-file-height="2834" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cape_Verde_Sal_pool.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A resort in <a href="/wiki/Sal,_Cape_Verde" title="Sal, Cape Verde">Sal</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Cape Verde's notable economic growth and improvement in living conditions despite a lack of natural resources has garnered <a href="#International_recognition">international recognition</a>, with other countries and international organizations often providing <a href="/wiki/Development_aid" title="Development aid">development aid</a>. Since 2007, Cape Verde has been classified as a <a href="/wiki/Developing_country" title="Developing country">developing nation</a>.</p>
<p>Cape Verde has few <a href="/wiki/Natural_resource" title="Natural resource">natural resources</a>. Only five of the ten main islands (Santiago, Santo Ant√£o, S√£o Nicolau, Fogo, and Brava) normally support significant agricultural production,<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup> and over 90% of all food consumed in Cape Verde is imported. Mineral resources include salt, <a href="/wiki/Pozzolana" title="Pozzolana">pozzolana</a> (a volcanic rock used in cement production), and <a href="/wiki/Limestone" title="Limestone">limestone</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bn_9-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bn-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> Its small number of wineries making Portuguese-style wines have traditionally focused on the domestic market, but have recently met with some international acclaim. A number of wine tours of Cape Verde's various microclimates began to be offered in spring 2010 and can be arranged through the tourism office.</p>
<p>The economy of Cape Verde is service-oriented, with commerce, transport, and public services accounting for more than 70% of <a href="/wiki/GDP" title="GDP" class="mw-redirect">GDP</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Although nearly 35% of the population lives in rural areas, agriculture and fishing contribute only about 9% of GDP. Light <a href="/wiki/Manufacturing" title="Manufacturing">manufacturing</a> accounts for most of the remainder. Fish and shellfish are plentiful, and small quantities are <a href="/wiki/Export" title="Export">exported</a>. Cape Verde has cold storage and freezing facilities and <a href="/wiki/Fish_processing" title="Fish processing">fish processing</a> plants in Mindelo, Praia, and on Sal. Expatriate Cape Verdeans contribute an amount estimated at about 20% of GDP to the domestic economy through <a href="/wiki/Remittance" title="Remittance">remittances</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bn_9-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bn-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> In spite of having few natural resources and being semi-desert, the country boasts the highest living standards in the region, and has attracted thousands of immigrants of different nationalities.</p>
<p>Since 1991, the government has pursued market-oriented economic policies, including an open welcome to <a href="/wiki/Foreign_investors" title="Foreign investors" class="mw-redirect">foreign investors</a> and a far-reaching <a href="/wiki/Privatization" title="Privatization">privatization</a> programme. It established as top development priorities the promotion of a <a href="/wiki/Market_economy" title="Market economy">market economy</a> and of the private sector; the development of <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Cape_Verde" title="Tourism in Cape Verde">tourism</a>, light manufacturing industries, and fisheries; and the development of <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Cape_Verde" title="Transport in Cape Verde">transport</a>, <a href="/wiki/Communications_in_Cape_Verde" title="Communications in Cape Verde" class="mw-redirect">communications</a>, and energy facilities. From 1994 to 2000 about $407 million in foreign investments were made or planned, of which 58% were in tourism,<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup> 17% in industry, 4% in infrastructure, and 21% in fisheries and services.<sup id="cite_ref-bn_9-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bn-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 2011, on four islands a windfarm was built that in total supplies about 30% of the electricity of the country. It is one of the top countries for renewable energy.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Between 2000 and 2009, <a href="/wiki/Real_GDP" title="Real GDP" class="mw-redirect">real GDP</a> increased on average by over 7 percent a year, well above the average for Sub-Saharan countries and faster than most small island economies in the region. Strong economic performance was bolstered by one of the fastest growing tourism industries in the world, as well as by substantial capital inflows that allowed Cape Verde to build up national currency reserves to the current 3.5 months of imports. Unemployment has been falling rapidly, and the country is on track to achieve most of the UN Millennium Development Goals ‚Äì including halving its 1990 poverty level.</p>
<p>In 2007, Cape Verde joined the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">World Trade Organization</a> (WTO) and in 2008 the country graduated from <a href="/wiki/Least_developed_country" title="Least developed country">Least Developed Country</a> (LDC) to Middle Income Country (MIC) status.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Cape Verde has significant cooperation with Portugal at every level of the economy, which has led it to link its currency first to the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_escudo" title="Portuguese escudo">Portuguese escudo</a> and, in 1999, to the <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">euro</a>. On June 23, 2008 Cape Verde became the 153rd member of the WTO.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The minimum wage has been set at 11,000.00 Cape Verdean Escudos (CVE) monthly (equivalent to US$138 or 101 Euros) for the first time in Cape Verdean history, in August 2013. The national minimum wage went into full effect on January 1, 2014.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Development">Development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Verde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The European Commission's total allocation for the period of 2008‚Äì2013 foreseen for Cape Verde to address "poverty reduction, in particular in rural and periurban areas where women are heading the households, as well as good governance" amounts to ‚Ç¨54.1 million.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Verde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Cape_Verde" title="Tourism in Cape Verde">Tourism in Cape Verde</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mindelo_portogrande.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Mindelo_portogrande.jpg/300px-Mindelo_portogrande.jpg" width="300" height="197" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/aa/Mindelo_portogrande.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/aa/Mindelo_portogrande.jpg 2x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="262" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mindelo_portogrande.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Yachts in Porto Grande, Mindelo on the island of <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Vicente,_Cape_Verde" title="S√£o Vicente, Cape Verde">S√£o Vicente</a>. Tourism is a growing source of income on the islands.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Cape Verde's strategic location at the crossroads of mid-Atlantic air and sea lanes has been enhanced by significant improvements at <a href="/wiki/Mindelo" title="Mindelo">Mindelo</a>'s harbour (<a href="/wiki/Porto_Grande_Bay" title="Porto Grande Bay">Porto Grande</a>) and at <a href="/wiki/Am%C3%ADlcar_Cabral_International_Airport" title="Am√≠lcar Cabral International Airport">Sal's</a> and <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Mendes_International_Airport" title="Francisco Mendes International Airport">Praia's international airports</a>. A <a href="/wiki/Aristides_Pereira_International_Airport" title="Aristides Pereira International Airport">new international airport</a> was opened in <a href="/wiki/Boa_Vista,_Cape_Verde" title="Boa Vista, Cape Verde">Boa Vista</a> in December 2007, and on the island of S√£o Vicente, the newest international airport (<a href="/wiki/Ces%C3%A1ria_%C3%89vora_Airport" title="Ces√°ria √âvora Airport">Ces√°ria √âvora Airport</a>) in Cape Verde, was opened in late 2009. Ship repair facilities at Mindelo were opened in 1983.<sup id="cite_ref-bn_9-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bn-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The major ports are Mindelo and Praia, but all other islands have smaller port facilities. In addition to the international airport on Sal, <a href="/wiki/List_of_airports_in_Cape_Verde" title="List of airports in Cape Verde">airports</a> have been built on all of the inhabited islands. All but the airports on Brava and <a href="/wiki/Santo_Ant%C3%A3o,_Cape_Verde" title="Santo Ant√£o, Cape Verde">Santo Ant√£o</a> enjoy scheduled air service. The archipelago has 3,050&#160;km (1,895&#160;mi) of roads, of which 1,010&#160;km (628&#160;mi) are paved, most using <a href="/wiki/Cobblestone" title="Cobblestone">cobblestone</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bn_9-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bn-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The country's future economic prospects depend heavily on the maintenance of aid flows, the encouragement of tourism, remittances, outsourcing labour to neighbouring African countries, and the momentum of the government's development programme.<sup id="cite_ref-bn_9-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bn-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Society">Society</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Verde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Society">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Verde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Cape_Verdeans" title="Cape Verdeans">Cape Verdeans</a> and <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Cape_Verde" title="Demographics of Cape Verde">Demographics of Cape Verde</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cape-Verde-demography.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Cape-Verde-demography.png/350px-Cape-Verde-demography.png" width="350" height="206" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Cape-Verde-demography.png/525px-Cape-Verde-demography.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Cape-Verde-demography.png/700px-Cape-Verde-demography.png 2x" data-file-width="724" data-file-height="426" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cape-Verde-demography.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Cape Verde's population, (1961-2003).</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Pyramide_Cap-Vert.PNG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Pyramide_Cap-Vert.PNG/350px-Pyramide_Cap-Vert.PNG" width="350" height="243" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Pyramide_Cap-Vert.PNG/525px-Pyramide_Cap-Vert.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Pyramide_Cap-Vert.PNG/700px-Pyramide_Cap-Vert.PNG 2x" data-file-width="902" data-file-height="625" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Pyramide_Cap-Vert.PNG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Cape Verde's <a href="/wiki/Population_pyramid" title="Population pyramid">population pyramid</a>, 2005.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The official Census recorded that Cape Verde had a population of 512,096 in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup> A large proportion (236,000) of Cape Verdeans live on the main island, Santiago.<sup id="cite_ref-cvp_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cvp-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_groups">Ethnic groups</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Verde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Ethnic groups">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Cape Verde archipelago was uninhabited when the Portuguese discovered it in 1456. African slaves were brought to the islands to work on Portuguese plantations. Cape Verdeans are <a href="/wiki/Mulatto" title="Mulatto">mulattos</a> (<a href="/wiki/Mesti%C3%A7o" title="Mesti√ßo">mesti√ßos</a> in Portuguese), who have mixed African and European origins; another term is <a href="/wiki/Creole_peoples#Portuguese_Africa" title="Creole peoples">creole</a> meaning mixed black and white descent.</p>
<p>European ancestors include Spanish and Italian seamen who were granted land by the Portuguese Empire, followed by Portuguese settlers, exiles, Portuguese Muslims and Portuguese Jews who were both victims of the Inquisition. Many foreigners from other parts of the world settled in Cape Verde as their permanent country. Most of them were Dutch, French, British and Arab (from Lebanon and Morocco), Chinese (especially from Ma√ßau), India, Indonesia, South America, American and Brazilian (including people of Portuguese and African descent). All of these have been absorbed into the mesti√ßo population.</p>
<p>Cape Verde's population in the 21st century is mostly <a href="/wiki/Creole_peoples#Portuguese_Africa" title="Creole peoples">creole</a>; the capital city <a href="/wiki/Praia" title="Praia">Praia</a> accounts for a quarter of the country's population. Over 65% of the population in the archipelago lives in urban centers, and the literacy rate is around 87% (i.e., 91% among men aged 15 and above and 83% among women aged 15 and above) according to the 2013 Cape Verdean census.</p>
<p>A genetic study revealed that the ancestry of the population in Cape Verde is predominantly European in the male line and West African in the female line; counted together the percentage is 56% African and 44% European.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup> The high degree of genetic and ethnic mixture of individuals is a result of centuries of migration. It is not unusual to encounter persons with dark skin and blond hair and blue eyes, and persons with light skin and black hair.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Verde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Cape Verde's official language is Portuguese. It is the language of instruction and government.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Cape_Verdean_Creole" title="Cape Verdean Creole">Cape Verdean Creole</a> is used colloquially and is the mother tongue of virtually all Cape Verdeans. Cape Verdean Creole or Kriolu is a dialect continuum of a Portuguese-based <a href="/wiki/Creole_language" title="Creole language">creole</a>. There is a substantial body of literature in Creole, especially in the <a href="/wiki/Santiago_Creole" title="Santiago Creole">Santiago Creole</a> and the <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Vicente_Creole" title="S√£o Vicente Creole">S√£o Vicente Creole</a>. Creole has been gaining prestige since the nation's independence from Portugal.</p>
<p>The differences between the forms of the language within the islands have been a major obstacle in the way of standardization of the language. Some people have advocated the development of two standards: a North (Barlavento) standard, centered on the S√£o Vicente Creole, and a South (Sotavento) standard, centered on the Santiago Creole. Manuel Veiga, PhD, a linguist and Minister of Culture of Cape Verde, is the premier proponent of Kriolu's officialization and standardization.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Verde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
